  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_47cc86bd-837a-4323-9495-82f1a62ba6ca'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText2878927304717597599" style="display:none">"Today is my last day as Violet Lasting. Tomorrow I become Lot 197."<br /><br />The Jewel is a shocking and compelling new YA series from debut author, Amy Ewing.<br /><br />Sold for six million diamantes, Violet is now Surrogate of the House of the Lake in the centre of the Lone City, the Jewel. Her sole purpose is to produce a healthy heir for the Duchess – a woman Violet fears and despises. <br /><br />Violet is trapped in a living death, her name and body no longer her own. She fights to hold on to her own identity and sanity, uncertain of the fate of her friends, isolated and at the mercy of the Duchess.<br /><br />The Handmaid's Tale meets The Other Boleyn Girl in a world where beauty and brutality collide.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5284503750041140254"><b>DNF at 95%, because I just don't give a fuck.</b><blockquote>
  <i>My frail resolve wavers. I think about what sort of person I want to be. I owe Lucien my life, and I will be loyal to him until the end. But Ash has nothing to do with that. Ash is separate, a part of my life that is just mine. There are things that are bigger than us, it’s true. Saving the surrogates. Destroying the royalty. Is loving Ash worth the risk?</i>
</blockquote>You get one fucking guess. What do you think she chooses?<br/><br/>This book is called <i>The Jewel</i>. It is </span>
  <span id="freeText5284503750041140254" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 95%, because I just don't give a fuck.</b><blockquote>
  <i>My frail resolve wavers. I think about what sort of person I want to be. I owe Lucien my life, and I will be loyal to him until the end. But Ash has nothing to do with that. Ash is separate, a part of my life that is just mine. There are things that are bigger than us, it’s true. Saving the surrogates. Destroying the royalty. Is loving Ash worth the risk?</i>
</blockquote>You get one fucking guess. What do you think she chooses?<br><br>This book is called <i>The Jewel</i>. It is a misnomer, because <b>had the title been accurate to the contents of the book, it would have been called <i>The Big, Stinking Pile of Shit.</i></b><br><br>This book is similar to Margaret Atwood's <i>The Handmaid's Tale</i> if it had been written for people who loved pretty dresses, Mary Sues, and hates being offended. In short, it's for people who watch Fox News.<br><br><i>The Handmaid's Tale</i> is a true dystopia in which the ruling class keeps a group of women around, solely for reproductive purposes. The main character in that book is a breeding cow. There is where the similarity ends. This book had none of the complexity, an interesting setting that <b>quickly descends into absurdity</b> and a character who is <b>bred for perfection...a pretty breeding cow, chosen for her genetic superiority.</b> The difference is that every ounce of flavor, every bit of grittiness, every iota of realism, every implication of the dark side of surrogacy and sexual abuse has been bleached the fuck out of this so-called <i>dystopia.</i><br><br><b>What's left is a flavorless, bland, utterly insipid "dystopian" version of every Mary Sue-insta-love you can ever imagine.</b><br><br><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>My skin is ivory, an odd contrast with my hair color, and my eyes are violet. I don’t need a mirror to tell me that. They’re what I was named for.</i>
</blockquote>Our heroine is the <b>fantastically-named <i>Violet Lasting</i></b>, who I will henceforce address as the html color code of <b>#800080, the code for purple.</b> Why? Because I can't type Violet Lasting without gagging, that's why.<br><br>In this Dystopian world, we have regions known as <b>The Farm, The Smoke, The Bank.</b> Each region has a ruler, a countess, a duchess...Due to some kind of genetic mutation, the upper class <b>are no longer able to bear children.</b> It would be an unusual world except for the <b>stupid fucking fact that almost everyone is named after a theme.</b> For example, all the people in one region are <b>named after colors.</b> Here are a sample of the names: Ochre, Hazel, Sable, Violet, Raven, Cobalt, Crow, Ginger. THERE ARE ONLY SO MANY COLORS, PEOPLE. YOU'RE GOING TO RUN OUT OF THEM EVENTUALLY.<br><br>Which is why I've decided to name our Violet #800080.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416023333i/11878046.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So no normal pregnancies for the rich here. Instead, they get genetically blessed girl like #800080 to have babies for them. But rather than being forced to go through, like, sexual abuse and stuff like that, these girls are <b>more or less pets for the family that buys them.</b> They are slaves, exquisitely dressed slaves, extraordinaryly pampered...sometimes abused---slaves. Not to mention breeding mares, who never have to have sex. EVER! Whoo! Totally PG, y'all. And the painful, excruciating, lengthy process of in-vitro fertilization? Turned into an artificial gloss of pain, without any authentic feeling of violation or despair.<br><br>In any case, #800080 is beautiful. Extraordinarily talented. Exceptionally lovely. In an auction of 200 girls, the highest ranked is the most beautiful, the most prized. #800080 is ranked...<blockquote>
  <i>I exhale. “197.”<br>Raven grins. “Looks like we’re hot commodities.”</i>
</blockquote>#800080 is bought by one of the wealthiest rulers, an extraordinary woman, <b>The Duchess,</b> for an unheard-of price.<blockquote>
  <i>“Sold!” the auctioneer cries, and all my muscles turn to jelly. “Sold for six million diamantes. To the Duchess of the Lake.”</i>
</blockquote>And #800080 is so fucking perfect, so brilliant, so smart. So excellent at the magical art of Augury (wut lol), that for the Duchess, she is a prize beyond compare.<blockquote>
  <i>“Yes,” the Duchess murmurs, almost to herself. “I think you are exactly what I’ve been looking for."<br><br>“Yes . . .” The Duchess runs a manicured finger down her cheek. “I’ve been waiting for you,” she says, her dark eyes fixed on mine. “For nineteen years.</i>
</blockquote>#80080 has the most dreadful existence in the world. #800080 can't believe the injustice of it all. Her body is not her own. She is a slave, a possession, there to be used, abused, and thrown away.<br><br>Horrifying. But then...Cora gets the chance <b>to do something about it. There is a secret rebellion that could free the entire fate of her fellow caged brood mares. She can free herself.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“She must believe you are on her side. You have to make her trust you. It is our best chance of getting you out as quickly and safely as possible.”</i>
</blockquote>So naturally, with this grand plot in mind, #800080 must focus all her energy on <b>looking at her lovely reflection.</b><blockquote>
  <i>The stranger in the mirror has been transformed.<br>I blink rapidly, trying to reconcile her with the image I had of myself in my head. The image of a pretty girl, slightly plump, full face, big eyes. The woman I am looking at now is beautiful. Stunning. Her cheeks seem thinner, molded to accent her high cheekbones, and her eyebrows arch delicately over luminous eyes, lined in rich purple with accents of lilac and gold. Her lips are glossed in pale pink, and her hair tumbles over her shoulders in thick curls, one side pinned up with a jeweled clip, encrusted with amethysts that form the shape of a butterfly. There is a shimmer to her skin, almost like she’s glowing.</i>
</blockquote>Exploring her enormous wardrobe. Wearing glamorous new nightgowns<blockquote>
  <i>I’m wearing a white silk nightdress, not unlike the one I wore at Southgate, embroidered with green and gold thread. The lady-in-waiting holds up a jade dressing gown, and I slip into it. Now I match this room.</i>
</blockquote>Wearing lovely dresses.<blockquote>
  <i>At five to seven, I stand outside the doors to the ballroom dressed in a pale green gown that makes the footman’s eyes pop before he can stop himself. The bodice leaves my shoulders bare, and the skirt falls to the floor in layers like the petals of a flower, their edges woven with glittering crystals. A choker of diamonds wraps around my neck and diamond earrings hang from my ears.</i>
</blockquote>And making judgmental calls on other people wearing beautiful dresses.<blockquote>
  <i>“My goodness, isn’t she just a vision,” the Electress gushes. She wears a gown of rich crimson velvet with a large dragon embroidered on its skirts—it seems like too much material for her small frame—and her lips are painted bright red. Like at the Auction, I am strongly reminded of a child playing dress-up.</i>
</blockquote>#800080 is powerful, her magic in Augury is strong. She can change the world. <b>Or she can explore the palatial mansion in which she is imprisoned.</b>I want to explore a little more of this palace on my own, decide for myself where to go and what to see. Several maids are cleaning the windows that look out onto the garden, and I flit past the doors, pausing in between them to make sure I’m not seen.With so much power, so much strength, that is being built up and trained every day, #80080 can do extraordinary things.<blockquote>
  <i>Standing in the doorway is a boy. Not a boy, a young man—he looks to be about the same age as the Duchess’s son. Tall and slender, with tousled brown hair and a strong jaw. His mouth curves a bit at the corners, like he’s holding back a smile. One hand rests in the pocket of his pants and his shirt is open at the collar.<br>But it’s his eyes that have me pinned in place. They are a soft gray-green, and they look at me in a way I haven’t been looked at since I started my life in the Jewel—like I am a girl, a person, not a surrogate. And yet, it’s something more than that; they look at me in a way that makes me feel hollow and strangely buzzy.</i>
</blockquote>Things like...fall into <b>insta-love.</b> Beautiful Boy <b>Ash</b> is a slave himself. He is a <b>companion</b>, a sexual boy toy to wealthy, older woman (who are, naturally, disgusting and nasty and so unlike the pure, beautiful, and virgin-Mary-like #800080). Together, they are not strong. Together, they are a danger. This is forbidden love, if there ever was one. He could be severely punished if they were caught. She could be killed at the Duchess' whim. And forget about her <b>grand rescue mission.</b><br><br>So what does <b>Romeo and #800080 do?</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Violet,” he says, and when he looks in my eyes, my stomach somersaults. “I think . . . I think I love you.”<br>I feel myself dissolve into a thousand molecules, amazed at how three small words can completely alter my state of being.<br>“I think I love you, too,” I whisper.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5284503750041140254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_950074759" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950074759" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950074759?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=instalove">instalove</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=the-chosen-one">the-chosen-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=painful-narration">painful-narration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=meh-romance">meh-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=confusing-plotline">confusing-plotline</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=stupid-heroes-heroines">stupid-heroes-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=what-the-hell">what-the-hell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950074759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10650199722672481647">A place where noble women cannot reproduce.<br/><br/>A place where these women buy beautiful, talented, peasant girls from the Auction.<br/><br/>A place where these teenage girls are bought to become surrogates.<br/><br/>A place where these  surrogates have unfathomable powers that change shapes, colors, and sizes.<br/><br/>...<br/><br/><strong>Is it me or are dystopian novels getting weirder and weirder every year? Either the world's running out of ideas and isgrasping at straws, or the world's trends have moved on ahead of me, 'cause I do not get it </strong></span>
  <span id="freeText10650199722672481647" style="display:none">A place where noble women cannot reproduce.<br><br>A place where these women buy beautiful, talented, peasant girls from the Auction.<br><br>A place where these teenage girls are bought to become surrogates.<br><br>A place where these  surrogates have unfathomable powers that change shapes, colors, and sizes.<br><br>...<br><br><strong>Is it me or are dystopian novels getting weirder and weirder every year? Either the world's running out of ideas and isgrasping at straws, or the world's trends have moved on ahead of me, 'cause I do not get it and I feel like an old woman now.</strong><br><br>In any case, I read this book with a <em>very</em> open mind. I was having weird feelings about the premise initially, but I still wanted to give it a chance just in case it did have the potential to be a blockbuster. It started okay, a bit confusing at first, but around the thirty percent mark it started spiraling down the rabbit hole for me. I was really, <em>really</em> struggling, but I trudged on, hoping to find something that would make me appreciate it. Unfortunately, the romance (read: insta-love to the max) entered, annoyed and enraged every fiber and nerve of my being, and <em>The Jewel</em> never manged to resurface from the abyss since then.<br><br>That left me very, very grumpy.<br><br>Now, don't get me wrong. The writing was decent. There were times it was vivid, and it was definitely easy to read. Unfortunately, we see the story unfold in the MC's eyes who is oh-so special and frankly, quite boring to boot, so while the writing may have had potential, it left a lot to be desired.<br><br><strong>Meet Violet, a determined, beautiful girl who has... violet eyes</strong>. Can it <em>not</em> get any more cheesy than that? For some otherworldly reason, aside from having such a rare color of eyes, she is also incredibly talented in Auguries, a kind of magic teenage girls like her have, that give them the ability to change colors (like making the painted skin in a portrait green), shapes and sizes/life (?) (like making a bud turn into a sapling or flower). And oh, before I forget, she also is the most sought-after surrogate in the Auction. <strong>We are repeatedly told of how special she is - from her looks, to her talents, to her playing the Cello - but we're not given much foundation aside from that, and we are simply expected to accept her awesomeness. </strong><br><br><strong>And may I say that she is so dull?</strong> She never really undergoes any substantial character development throughout, and she is so monotonous in her narration. I guess that's to be expected from someone who is groomed to be a surrogate, but come on, we're in her thoughts, man! This is the chance to give her some spine and personality! Some <em>oomph</em> in her bones! But nooooope - Violet (who has violet eyes... man, I just can't get over that) has to be a one-dimensional twit.<br><br><strong>And nothing really happens. For 95% of the bloody book, nothing really happens.</strong> The MC eats breakfast, gets sneered at by the Duchess, plays music, walks around the mansion, wears dresses, gets sneered at by the Duchess, attends balls, goes to the doctor for check-ups and experiments, gets sneered at by the Duchess, attends balls, wears dresses, plays music... And oh, gets complimented at for being so awesome, beautiful, extraordinary, and talented between the activities, while wallowing in self-pity. It felt so damn repetitive. There would be twists introduced here and there, but they were written in such an anti-climactic way that the best it got from me was a yawn.<br><br><strong>So, was I surprised when something <em>did</em> bloody happen, it gets cut IN THE MIDDLE OF THINGS and now we have to wait for the next book?</strong> Dude. Just... what the hell. There are <strong>cliffhangers</strong>, where the book ends with a question or an event but STILL giving us a proper ending to an arc of the story, and there are <strong>ANNOYING CLIFFHANGERS</strong>, like the one incorporated here, where something is happening and then it gets cut in the middle. FUCK.<br><br>AND DON'T GET ME STARTED ON THE ROMANCE. ARGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGGH.<br><br>One word: instalove. INSTA-BLOODY-LOVE.<br><br><strong>It made me rant, rage, and swear exotic curses in my mind.</strong> I'm telling you, folks, you wouldn't want a peek into my brain during that span of time lest you want to escort me to the authorities. It was one of the worst and fast-paced romances I've ever read, and that's saying something.<br><br>Imagine, the first meeting that they had where they talk a bit about music and where it ends with him being rude to her and she tells him this:<br><blockquote>
  <em>"I've never met anyone like you before," I say. I blush furiously - that didn't come out the way I'd intended.</em>
</blockquote><br>That very night, as in JUST A FEW HOURS LATER, she's saying this:<br><blockquote>
  <em>I stare at my reflection - pink cheeks, tiny smile, bright eyes... the girl in the mirror looks truly happy, for the first time.</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>I've never thought much about kissing, but the idea of Ash's lips against mine --</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>I giggle.</em>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408469415ra/10854496.gif" alt="" width="500" height="206" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>AND IT DOESN'T END THERE! </b>When she sees him at dinner, she goes:<br><blockquote>
  <em>It's only been a couple of hours since I met him, but he's somehow even more handsome than I remember. My whole body feels like it's blushing.</em>
</blockquote><br>Are your eyes twitching yet? HAHAHAHA BUT I'M NOT DONE YET. When Ash promptly ignores her, she now goes:<br><blockquote>
  <em>The pain of this is a sharp, physical thing, almost like the aftermath of an Augury except that it's not my head that feels like needles are being shoved into it.</em>
</blockquote><br>Jesus, girl... I would understand if you've known each other for some time already, but you don't - you just met him a few hours ago. A FEW HOURS AGO!!!!!! It's not that serious, darling! Believe it or not, it isn't!<br><br><strong>And in their third meeting, apparently, the guy can't stop thinking of her either!</strong> And then, they kiss. And soon after a few more fumblings, they tell each other the following:<br><blockquote>
  <em>"I think I love you"</em>
  <br>
  <br>
  <em>"I want you forever, Ash."</em>
</blockquote><br>And I was:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408469415ra/10854497.gif" alt="" width="500" height="375" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously, this would have been more bearable if the romance felt more natural. It moved way too fast for my tastes. They keep saying they see <em>something</em> in each other, but I never read enough that could justify the feelings they had. It felt so superficial and it was hard for me to regard it seriously. It was far from beautiful, it was far from deep. To me, they looked like rabbits in heat that just wanted to get it on already. EAGER BEAVERS MUCH?!<br><br><strong>And the world-building is absolutely shaky</strong>. The kingdom or whatever is divided into rings, where there's the FARM (where I guess the farmers live...??), and there's the MARSH (where... some kind of people live... x_x), there's the SMOKE (where there are the factories... I guess?), the BANK (where there are merchants) and the JEWEL or where the nobles live, and each quadrant (North, South, East, West) there are holding facilities for girls like Violet (who have bloody violet eyes...) where they are trained to be surrogates. For some reason, the nobles can't have babies so they hold Auctions, where girls go to the highest bidder. And oh, the nobles with fight each other through some sort of court intrigue. Aaaaaand that's it.<br><br>The Farm, the Marsh, the Smoke, the Bank and the Jewel. And those descriptions. Not enough atmosphere or anything. Although there is some history with regards to the how the noble houses came to be today, but I'm pretty sure the world-building isn't limited to that.<br><br><strong>Overall, this book had the potential, but the </strong><strong>awesome self-pitying girl and the shaky world-building and the migraine-induing romance made me want to scream out loud</strong>. If you liked <i>The Selection </i>you may like it, as some reviewers pointed out that the feel is quite similar. I still encourage you to try it out for yourself to see if it works for you. This seems to be more of a hit-or-miss book, judging by the mixed reviews that are posted right now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10650199722672481647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_890311852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890311852" />
    <a title="Fenia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18261002-fenia"><img alt="Fenia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474522538p2/18261002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890311852?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fenia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fenia" href="/user/show/18261002-fenia">Fenia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406347494" href="/book/show/22586252-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18261002-fenia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

<div id="review_853211938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/853211938" />
    <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always"><img alt="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562987681p2/5478965.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/853211938?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always" href="/user/show/5478965-aimee-aimee-always">Aimee ♥ | Aimee, Always</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=romances-i-cant-understand">romances-i-cant-understand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=i-am-not-pleased-with-that-cliffie">i-am-not-pleased-with-that-cliffie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=no-chemistry">no-chemistry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=insta-love-lust-attraction">insta-love-lust-attraction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=oh-the-fluff">oh-the-fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=let-me-gouge-your-eyeballs-out">let-me-gouge-your-eyeballs-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=ending-sucked">ending-sucked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5478965-aimee-aimee-always?shelf=eye-roll">eye-roll</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer853211938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3156926919726268810"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408461244i/10853780._SX540_.png' width='400px' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Another example of wasted potential,<strong><em> The Jewel</em> could have been the next big thing for many other readers--if not for that shitty, awful romance</strong>. That's pretty bad, considering I almost NEVER say something is <em>awful</em>--I call a lot of things <em>shitty</em>, but <em>awful</em>? That is a hundred times worse than<em> shitty</em> in the Language of Aimee.<br/><br/>Oh, and noticed how I said "many other readers"? Yes, because even without said shitty, awful romance, this book is just not for me. It was a bit similar to <em>The Hunger Game</em></span>
  <span id="freeText3156926919726268810" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408461244i/10853780._SX540_.png" width="400px" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Another example of wasted potential,<strong><em> The Jewel</em> could have been the next big thing for many other readers--if not for that shitty, awful romance</strong>. That's pretty bad, considering I almost NEVER say something is <em>awful</em>--I call a lot of things <em>shitty</em>, but <em>awful</em>? That is a hundred times worse than<em> shitty</em> in the Language of Aimee.<br><br>Oh, and noticed how I said "many other readers"? Yes, because even without said shitty, awful romance, this book is just not for me. It was a bit similar to <em>The Hunger Games</em> (they had rings around the city and the larger rings are for the poorer sectors) and <em>The Selection</em> (the atmosphere and writing), but<strong> there were really just some stupid things I couldn't understand about this one</strong>. *grabs notes* Let's get started, friends.<br><br><blockquote>"I have absolutely no idea what it must be like to be pregnant."</blockquote><br><br>What. The. Hell? Weren't these girls brought up to be surrogates in the future? Why does it seem like Violet seem to have zero idea about pregnancy? <strong>Throughout the novel, she was basically ignorant and constantly confused</strong>--just SNAP OUT OF IT AND GET A GRIP ON YOURSELF, OKAY?<br><br>This novel was also had <strong>a billion cliche scenes/lines</strong>. I mean, how many times have you read about the girl "in the mirror" as she "transformed"? That's seriously one of the most annoying bookish scenes ever, and I can't help but cringe every time I read about those.<br><br>And drama. Drama llamas everywhere, people! <strong><em>The Jewel</em> could totally be turned into the next <em>High School Musical</em>.</strong> Really, the characters have already practiced! See:<br><br><blockquote>Her voice is sweet and she sings a traditional Marsh-song, one we all know.<br>[...]<br>Two other girls join in.</blockquote><br><br>And here we go: the romance. Excuse me while I go laugh hysterically, folks! Because this romance gave me a huge migraine. I feel like vomiting just thinking about it. But still, I present to you <strong>THE STAGES OF THE ROMANCE IN <em>THE JEWEL</em>! </strong>(Take note that the novel is only about 350 pages long, so these are actually really close to each other.)<br><br>1. They meet. They lock eyes. What can Violet say about Ash's eyes? "[T]hey look at me in a way that makes me feel hollow and strangely buzzy." (51% in the eARC)<br>2. When Violet leaves Ash's room, she thinks of kissing him. (53.8% in the eARC)<br>3. A few hours after they first met, when they meet again, Violet says, "My whole body feels like it's blushing." (54.3% in the eARC<br>4. First kiss. (70.7% in the eARC)<br>5. Second kiss. (73.9% in the eARC)<br>6. Admission of love. (85.7% in the eARC)<br>7. <s>They get married, ride off into the sunset and have babies. (Hopefully NEVER.)</s><br><br>Okay, I should get over that. Moving on!<br><br>This book also had some fantasy elements mixed in. I did appreciate that, since fantasy <em>is</em> my favorite genre, but <strong>I still have many unanswered questions in my mind about the magic and sorcery</strong> in this book. Well, I had questions about ALMOST EVERYTHING, actually. Why were there surrogates? How come only magic-wielding girls can be surrogates? <strong>I also felt like the fantasy aspect of the novel was just forced into it</strong>--it didn't really seem to fit with the mood of the story, but maybe that's just me.<br><br>One last thing: <strong>STEREOTYPING</strong>. Women were portrayed as either too helpless and idiotic (Violet) or vicious and bitchy (basically all of the women who bought surrogates). Men were portrayed as handsome and always drunk (Garnet--the only character I could tolerate) or kind gentlemen (Ash--*pukes*). Where are the normal, average, REALISTIC people?<br><br><strong>The only positive thing I can say about the book is that I did enjoy Ewing's writing</strong>. It was easy to read and I just flew through the pages without much reading-related problems.<br><br>Well, this review turned out a lot longer than I planned. Anyway, I'm off to bleach my brain after re-thinking about this novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3156926919726268810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1035842501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1035842501" />
    <a title="Lindsay Cummings" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4729981-lindsay-cummings"><img alt="Lindsay Cummings" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442622890p2/4729981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1035842501?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay Cummings" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay Cummings" href="/user/show/4729981-lindsay-cummings">Lindsay Cummings</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1035842501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8186113969926839678">My first thought about THE JEWEL was that the gorgeous silver cover was strangely similar to the covers for THE SELECTION series. I wasn't sure, after reading the synopsis, if this book would also have a similar plot. I was totally wrong.<br/><br/>In one word, THE JEWEL is FANTASTIC. When I began reading, I was pleasantly surprised by the writing style and the very xmen like twist that this "ball gown" story took on. THE JEWEL is brilliant and unique, and so creepy in the way the society is run, that I fo</span>
  <span id="freeText8186113969926839678" style="display:none">My first thought about THE JEWEL was that the gorgeous silver cover was strangely similar to the covers for THE SELECTION series. I wasn't sure, after reading the synopsis, if this book would also have a similar plot. I was totally wrong.<br /><br />In one word, THE JEWEL is FANTASTIC. When I began reading, I was pleasantly surprised by the writing style and the very xmen like twist that this "ball gown" story took on. THE JEWEL is brilliant and unique, and so creepy in the way the society is run, that I found myself unable to put it down. I flew through all 368 pages in just a few days (in the middle of a huge move and edit, as well--- it was that good!).<br /><br />In Violet Lasting's world, identity isn't important. She's not a name; she's just a number. As a surrogate, raised to bear a child for whatever member of the royal Jewel section of society purchases her in an auction, Violet has been trained for years to be submissive and poised and perfectly fine with being in the background. <br /><br />The twist to this story comes with something called the Auguries: special powers that each surrogate has, where they can change the colors and shapes of objects, as well as grow things. In Violet's case, the third augury, Growth, is her best gift.<br /><br />When Violet is taken to the auction and purchased by the Duchess of the Lake, she's thrown into a world full of fancy balls and mansions and dresses and makeup. But there's a dark side to Violet's new, glittering world.<br /><br />There's death. There's destruction. There are lies and manipulations, and somehow, very well-twisted into the middle of it all, is forbidden love.<br /><br />Violet soon discovers that she can never be who she truly wants to be. Danger is around every corner. Love is not an option. And when Violet discovers she might have a way out, even darker secrets are revealed. The characters are wonderfully fleshed out, from Violet herself, to her fellow surrogate and best friend Raven, to the horrible Duchess of the Lake. Even Violet's maid, Annabelle, a girl who can't speak, was so well done that I felt like I knew her. The love interest, Ashe, is totally shiptastic.<br /><br />This story is just incredible. I fell in love with it, and by the time I finished (warning: there's a cliffhanger!), it was 1am and I was dying for book 2.<br /><br />THE JEWEL is definitely not a copy of any other story---it stands out on its own, and is sure to be a bestseller. Fantastic. I loved the terrifying, beautiful world that Amy Ewing created. I need book 2 now! (And I've preordered my own hardcover copy for my personal shelves!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8186113969926839678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer853995094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10045931900122667219"><b>9/30/17 - ON SALE for $1.99:</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.amazon.com/Jewel-Book-1-ebook/dp/B00H7LW82S/ref=as_li_ss_il?s=digital-text&ie=UTF8&qid=1504982462&sr=1-5&linkCode=li1&tag=rabrea-20&linkId=00a3633de58c128b93a22dbff1e642e4' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483538220i/21622429.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483538220i/21622430.gif' width='1' height='1' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://amzn.to/2gRVBRY'>http://amzn.to/2gRVBRY</a><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/08/early-review-the-jewel-by-amy-ewing.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Violet Lasting is a Surrogate. She lives in a world where blue bloods can no longer produce viable offspring. BUT. Before they begin to die out, a doctor discovers a genetic quirk that (fortuitously) exists most frequently in the lowest caste of their society . . . a quirk that allows the girls who have it to carry a royal child to term . . . <br/><br/>And so it is mandatory--on pain of death--for every girl to be teste</span>
  <span id="freeText10045931900122667219" style="display:none"><b>9/30/17 - ON SALE for $1.99:</b><br><br><a href="https://www.amazon.com/Jewel-Book-1-ebook/dp/B00H7LW82S/ref=as_li_ss_il?s=digital-text&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1504982462&amp;sr=1-5&amp;linkCode=li1&amp;tag=rabrea-20&amp;linkId=00a3633de58c128b93a22dbff1e642e4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483538220i/21622429.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483538220i/21622430.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/2gRVBRY">http://amzn.to/2gRVBRY</a><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/08/early-review-the-jewel-by-amy-ewing.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>Violet Lasting is a Surrogate. She lives in a world where blue bloods can no longer produce viable offspring. BUT. Before they begin to die out, a doctor discovers a genetic quirk that (fortuitously) exists most frequently in the lowest caste of their society . . . a quirk that allows the girls who have it to carry a royal child to term . . . <br><br>And so it is mandatory--on pain of death--for every girl to be tested for this quirk upon reaching puberty. If the girl is a Surrogate, she is taken from her family to be raised, groomed, and educated for life in the Jewel.<br><br>But being a Surrogate means more than simply having a womb capable of playing host to a royal baby:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>The first time I coughed up blood, I thought I was dying. But it stops after a year or so. Now I only have the occasional nosebleed.</i>
</blockquote><br>Being a Surrogate also means being able to manipulate the three Auguries: color, shape, and growth. Having command of the first (and easiest) Augury means being about to change the superficial aspects of something like . . . wait for it . . . <i>color</i>. Same goes for the shape and growth Auguries, but the interesting thing here is that the royals who purchase their Surrogates at the Auction intend for the girls to use their gifts specifically on their child.<br><br>In utero.<br><br>Kind of cool. Kind of <i>creepy</i>.<br><br>Kind of dangerous for the Surrogate . . .<br><br>Or at least that was my early impression. Anything that causes severe headaches, nosebleeds, and coughing up blood cannot be good for you. BUT. Like I said, only the lower class has this ability, and everyone knows poor people have no power, so the upper classes are free to use them as they see fit.<br><br>I actually thought this was a clever premise. Anyone who has taken any kind of History of England (or any Western European country) knows about the weakness and illness that began to plague the royals, b/c of all the inbreeding. And in this <i>inexplicably</i> dystopian, <i>presumably</i> post-apocalyptic (b/c “Lone” city) world, who’s going to stop them from abusing their power and exploiting the peasants?<br><br>No one, that’s who.<br><br>There were lots of interesting little details that made this story stand out for me:<br><br><blockquote>1. Iron bars in the shape of roses on the windows of the facilities where the girls lived until it was time for their Auction.&lt;——beautifully ironic.<br><br>2. The use of real folk songs—I cannot hear or read the lyrics of “The Water is Wide” without getting goosebumps.<br><br>3. The flashback to the girl getting her head chopped off for trying to escape becoming a Surrogate gave me goosebumps too:</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <i>The girl was wild, long black hair tangled around her face, framing eyes of a brilliant, almost shocking, blue. There was something fierce and untamed about her appearance. She couldn’t have been more than a few years older than me.<br><br>She didn’t fight of struggle against the two Regimentals restraining her. She didn’t cry, or beg. She looked strangely peaceful. When they put her head on the block, I could swear she smiled. The magistrate asked her if she had any last words.<br><br>“This is how it begins,” she said. “I am not afraid.” Her face saddened, and she added, “Tell Cobalt I love him.”<br>Then they chopped off her head.</i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>4. Violet’s first cello performance . . . YEP, more goosebumps.<br><br>5. I’m sure there’s probably some female version of the male occupation of “companion” in this world, but in this story, it’s the male version in the spotlight, which is still terrible, but also refreshing somehow.<br><br>6. I saw that twist at the end coming, but it was still a very cool twist.</blockquote><br>BUT . . . there were even more things that were either strangely familiar, or did not work for me at all:<br><br><blockquote>1. The “inexplicable” and “presumably” parts of the world-building. We’re given no explanation for the lack of any other cities, or how this one manages to have marshland in concentric rings with the rolling hills and vineyards of farmland. Mighty convenient that . . .<br><br>2. Violet’s eyes are violet. This is a personal peeve of mine, b/c NO SUCH THING. No, not even Elizabeth Taylor. Her eyes were very, very blue, NOT purple. So. Unless it’s an alien or some type of Fae creature, if it has violet eyes, I’m going to roll mine.<br><br>3. If a noun isn’t named for exactly what it is, or some obvious attribute—industrial part of the city is called Smoke, farm part of the city is called Farm, Violet has violet eyes, etc.—it’s named some other animal, vegetable, or mineral. Raven and her twin brother Crow. The royals are all named after precious gems, or in one case, rare and expensive wood—Ebony. It’s weird and distracting.<br><br>4. Lucien is Violet’s very own Cinna. And yes, I realize that “Lucien” is not an animal, vegetable, or mineral, but he is also property, and I have suspicions about what his real name is.<br><br>5. The Surrogates have their own version of District Twelve’s three-fingered salute.<br><br>6. The “It only takes one small stone to start an avalanche,” and, “one crack spreads until the whole wall crumbles,” lesser versions of, “It only takes a spark.”<br><br>7. For a smart girl, Violet is incredibly dense sometimes. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ash is a freaking “companion.” What does she think he’s doing with Carnelian? AND how does she not consider the possibility that she could be pregnant with her own child after her shenanigans with Ash? ALSO, she doesn’t seem to pick up on the fact that the girl whose head she saw get chopped off was Lucien’s sister. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>8. The insta-love. It’s not as bad as most, but it is still, undeniably, insta-love.</blockquote><br>So yeah, there were problems. But overall it was an entertaining read with a great premise—I finished it in an afternoon—and I’ll definitely read the next book. Amy Ewing’s THE JEWEL is a solid first installment in her THE LONE CITY series. It combines fantasy and dystopian elements to create an interesting new whole, so if either of those sub-genres are your thing, I’d check this one out.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10045931900122667219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1309541542" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1309541542" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309541542?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062369000" href="/book/show/22138440-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=r2r-complete">r2r-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309541542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4271948508450900890">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Sometimes, I wish I hadn’t been born a surrogate.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434468510i/15226010._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was an enjoyable dystopian, with girls with special powers being sold as surrogates.<br/><br/>I felt quite sorry for Violet in this story, her whole life had been changed by one blood test, and she was forced to carry someone else’s baby after being sold at an auction. I did think that she made some very dubious decisions at </span>
  <span id="freeText4271948508450900890" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“Sometimes, I wish I hadn’t been born a surrogate.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434468510i/15226010._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was an enjoyable dystopian, with girls with special powers being sold as surrogates.<br><br>I felt quite sorry for Violet in this story, her whole life had been changed by one blood test, and she was forced to carry someone else’s baby after being sold at an auction. I did think that she made some very dubious decisions at times though, and she should probably have covered her tracks better than she did!<br><br><b>
  <i>“The thought of being pregnant, of having someone else’s child growing inside me, is terrifying.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434468510i/15226011.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was about Violet being sold as a surrogate, and being forced to demonstrate her powers over the ‘Auguries’ – being able to change somethings colour, change its shape, and encourage it to grow. I did think the world building was pretty good, even if it did remind me of other books, although I wondered why the surrogates didn’t use the Auguries more. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Violet really missed a trick with that pregnancy test! She could have used her powers to turn it green, making everyone think she was pregnant, and meaning that she could pretend for a couple of weeks and avoid them trying to impregnate her again during that time!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <i>“The lone city is divided into five circles, each separated by a wall, and all of them but the Marsh have nicknames based on their industry.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434468608i/15226028.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was a bit of a forbidden romance in this one, and it was a very bad idea really!<br><br><b>
  <i>“Then his mouth is on mine.<br>I feel entirely new.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434468608i/15226029._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was pretty good, and now I remember what happened I can start book 2! Yay!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433066772i/15045457.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>7 out of 10<br><br><br>How it ends - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ This is a giant spoiler, so don’t read unless you’ve already read this book! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <br>-	Lucien (a male lady-in-waiting) gives Violet the serum which will cause her to appear dead, and tells her to take it the next night. He will then retrieve her body, and make her disappear.<br>-	Violet sees Raven at a dinner party, and she is pregnant, and does not look well.<br>-	Raven collapses at the dinner table, and Violet decides to give the serum to her instead.<br>-	Violet then goes to visit Ash (the companion of her mistresses niece), and apologises to him for not being honest with him about what she was planning.<br>-	The Duchess catches Ash and Violet alone in his room, and has Ash knocked out and dragged off to the dungeons to await execution.<br>-	Violet is taken to her room where she uses the tuning fork which Lucien gave her to try and contact him, but instead her call is answered by Garnet, the Duchess’ own son.<br>-	The End. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4271948508450900890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1309541542">
  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer7718733657130544445">2.5 stars<br/><br/>I was sort of bored throughout the book. I'm thinking the subject matter just didn't interest me, so you might have a different experience with this one than I did.<br/>Fabulous cover, though!<br/><br/>The Royalty that live in the Jewel can't have babies anymore. <br/>Poor people, yes. Even make the child better looking, smarter, </span>
  <span id="freeText7718733657130544445" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br><br>I was sort of bored throughout the book. I'm thinking the subject matter just didn't interest me, so you might have a different experience with this one than I did.<br>Fabulous cover, though!<br><br>The Royalty that live in the Jewel can't have babies anymore. <br>Poor people, yes. Rich people, no.<br>But the nobility have found that some of the poor girls have these<i> abilities</i> that can allow them to manipulate a fetus in their wombs. Make it a viable pregnancy. Even make the child better looking, smarter, more talented, etc.. So, they test all of the poor girls as soon as they get their period, and if they have this <i>ability</i> then they whisk them off to be raised in solitude. Once there, they train them to use their powers, until they are old enough to be auctioned off to the highest bidder.<br><br>Violet is one of the surrogate girls, and she's about to be auctioned off when the story starts. The book goes on about how she is used and abused, her concern for her friend, what is expected of the surrogates, how they are treated as less than human....and so on.<br>Plod, plod, plod.<br><br>Of course, her abilities are <i>special</i>. More. Better. Something that hasn't been seen before.<br>I don't...I'm still not sure what the hell her abilities <i>are</i>, but it has something to do with the <i>life-force</i> of things. <br>Like, she makes plants grow and stuff?<br>Lots of pain, nosebleeds, and coughing up blood happen when their powers are used, by the way. Kinda gross when the girls are spewing blood all over the dinner table, you know? <br><i>*hoark*</i> <br><br>Plans are made to help her escape by a mysterious servant with a magical tuning fork.<br><i>No, really!</i><br>But before she can escape, she needs to fall in love with a boy, right? <br>Yes. Yes, she does.<br>Done! <br>Love is in the air, and it feels somewhat boring and rushed. <br>BUT. The main thing is that they desperately love each other, there will be horrifying repercussions if they are caught, and that she will act foolishly for love.<br>Ta-da!<br><br>The last 5 pages are excellent, and left me with a cliffhanger so good that I would almost consider reading the next book, just to see what happens next.<br>Yes, really.<br><br>It may be that I have read too many books with a similar feel to them, but this just didn't do it for me. However, that doesn't mean that I would warn anyone off of reading it, because it wasn't badly written.<br>Sorry, book.<br>It's not you, it's me.<br><br><div>

  </a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer977566156" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17388933076282058175">I think on some level I should probably have disliked this book, but I ended up enjoying it quite a bit. It's a light read and I sped through pretty fast and none of the characters irritated me too much. This might have something to do with the fact that books that explore a Reproductive Dystopian world fasciate me. I didn't really love the romance because it is on the "quick" side of things, but somehow that did not seem to bother me much. The plot seemed to more than make up for that, and <em>The </em></span>
  <span id="freeText17388933076282058175" style="display:none">I think on some level I should probably have disliked this book, but I ended up enjoying it quite a bit. It's a light read and I sped through pretty fast and none of the characters irritated me too much. This might have something to do with the fact that books that explore a Reproductive Dystopian world fasciate me. I didn't really love the romance because it is on the "quick" side of things, but somehow that did not seem to bother me much. The plot seemed to more than make up for that, and <em>The Jewel</em> had good pacing and even better anticipation. One thing you might want to consider is that this book does have a terrible cliffhanger. It's the worst. I know I'll end up reading book two just for that alone. I only hope that book two either expounds on the romance or gets rid of it completely.<br /><br />I can't compare this to <em>The Selection</em> because I haven't read it, so if you are looking for me to do that, I'm not the best person to ask.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16164745815296170268">Violet is a surrogate, born with unique gifts to shape the world around her, yet bought and sold to the highest bidder in a world where royalty rules all. This had a lot of flaws, and unfortunately it really hindered my enjoyment of what could have been a good story. <br/><br/>The main issue I had was just how unoriginal I found the story. Reading this felt like deja vu. Poor yet beautiful girl with unique gifts brought into a different world? Check. Evil ruling power that manipulates said girl? Check. Du</span>
  <span id="freeText16164745815296170268" style="display:none">Violet is a surrogate, born with unique gifts to shape the world around her, yet bought and sold to the highest bidder in a world where royalty rules all. This had a lot of flaws, and unfortunately it really hindered my enjoyment of what could have been a good story. <br /><br />The main issue I had was just how unoriginal I found the story. Reading this felt like deja vu. Poor yet beautiful girl with unique gifts brought into a different world? Check. Evil ruling power that manipulates said girl? Check. Dull and one dimensional love interest leading to instalove? Check. I also think I rolled my eyes several times over the names of some of these characters. One character is called Cinder. And her brother is Ash. Seriously. <br /><br />My other main issue was Ash. The love interest. The story takes a significant dip after his introduction, as he's so dull with no definable characteristics or charm. He's basically Finnick from The Hunger Games without the emotional depth. When Violet starts fawning over him after meeting him for all of ten minutes, I knew this story wasn't going to end the way I wanted it too. I much preferred the relationship between the various surrogates and their 'owners', and the dynamics and rivalries that are barely explored but had so much potential. I didn't think there was any need to introduced Ash at all. If anything, he hinders the plot. I found all of his scenes very cringy, and I often skim read them. Violet as a main character is also severely lacking in personality. She goes from petulant teen to submissive slave with no in-between. She's got no emotional depth, and bumbled from one scenario to the next, relying on other people to rescue her. <br /><br />Several times I was also confused by the world itself. We don't see anything outside of The Jewel except very briefly at the beginning. The rules of the world aren't explained very deeply either, and are often contradictory. Why treat some surrogates well, others badly, yet always have them dressed up like dolls all the time? Why are they repeatedly drugged? It felt like an easy cop out to explain any passage of time. What are the various Auguries, and why do only poor girls have these powers? They weren't explained well, or integrated well into the story, and I often felt confused when Violet uses any of them. Also, their use with regards to childbirth is just...odd. <br /><br />This really wasn't for me. The potential was there, but the execution fell flat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16164745815296170268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_949965154" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/949965154" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/949965154?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=arc-edelweiss">arc-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-aug-2014">zzread-aug-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer949965154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1810914296583396212">ARGHH! <br/><br/>It is not often that I give 1 star to a book. I usually try to find the good in each book that I read. Even books that I have not finished do not get a star rating, that's just how I review. But - this book drove me bonkers and I must highlight the things that drove me crazy.<br/><br/>1)This is a dystopian book along the lines of <b>The Selection</b> (which I haven't had the pleasure of reading, but the synopsis sounds right) and <b>The Handmaid's Tale</b> (of which there is absolutely no comparison). <br/><br/>2)Young wo</span>
  <span id="freeText1810914296583396212" style="display:none">ARGHH! <br /><br />It is not often that I give 1 star to a book. I usually try to find the good in each book that I read. Even books that I have not finished do not get a star rating, that's just how I review. But - this book drove me bonkers and I must highlight the things that drove me crazy.<br /><br />1)This is a dystopian book along the lines of <b>The Selection</b> (which I haven't had the pleasure of reading, but the synopsis sounds right) and <b>The Handmaid's Tale</b> (of which there is absolutely no comparison). <br /><br />2)Young women are groomed to become auctioned off as surrogates to the wealthy and privileged royalty of this world. They are given a lot number and dressed up in spectacular gowns and costumes and sold to the highest bidder. Sounds like slavery to me. Oh, the girls are never referred to by their names, only lot numbers. <br /><br />3)The women are treated like pets by their "owners." They are led about on a leash, told what to eat, what to do, and how to behave. Good behavior is rewarded, bad behavior is punished.<br /><br />4)There's a lot of invasive medical testing with our main character being drugged, poked, and prodded way too many times. <br /><br />5)Too much emphasis is placed on the beautiful dresses and gowns and balls. The reality is that this is a race to produce a super baby.<br /><br />6)There is a much more sinister aspect to this whole baby making process. Surrogates are told that once they produce a child, they will go on and retire in another part of this world. Wonder if that's true? Also, there is work to lobotomize the surrogates so they would just have a breeding womb available. Gross! <br /><br />7)The writing is weak. The story is told in first person POV, so we only know what Violet is doing or thinking. See my status updates for an example. <br /><br />8)Love triangle - is there or isn't there? Can't tell you for sure. Our heroin falls in love with a character, who is the love interest of another.<br /><br />9)Cliffhanger - If you hang on until the end, you'll be treated to a surprise cliffhanger. <br /><br />I'm sure that there will be plenty of people who will enjoy this book. For me, it was not a pleasant read. Read at your own risk.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to Edelweiss and HarperTeen for a review copy of this book.</i><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1810914296583396212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1037350393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer3206720071291404792">Hello. If you've found this review, perhaps you are wondering why I appear so irked by this book. Giving it one star, and all.<br/><br/>Well, it's because MARGARET ATWOOD already wrote this book. Also, the girl on the cover, yeah, she is way too well-dressed to be a slave.<br/><br/>Some books do not need a dumbed-down romance version with a bunch of silly tropes. The Handmaid's Tale is one of those books*. It is a serious treatment of a serious subject. Why is there a need to publish a glossy new version with girls</span>
  <span id="freeText3206720071291404792" style="display:none">Hello. If you've found this review, perhaps you are wondering why I appear so irked by this book. Giving it one star, and all.<br /><br />Well, it's because MARGARET ATWOOD already wrote this book. Also, the girl on the cover, yeah, she is way too well-dressed to be a slave.<br /><br />Some books do not need a dumbed-down romance version with a bunch of silly tropes. The Handmaid's Tale is one of those books*. It is a serious treatment of a serious subject. Why is there a need to publish a glossy new version with girls in pretty dresses?<br /><br />I have nothing against YA. I love YA. Some YA is wonderful. This book, though, this one has ALREADY BEEN WRITTEN. Read the fucking original. It will make you smarter.<br /><br />Thank you.<br /><br />*I just realized that they have made this a trilogy. A trilogy. Margaret Atwood was able to tell this story in a single, classic, amazing book that is still studied in high school and college courses. Why is this a trilogy? Are we now at the point where YA publishers are unable to publish anything that isn't a series?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1095975345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer43399518078934618">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>Mini review:</b><br/><br/>After the early reviews started rolling in for this one I was getting less and less excited about reading this one. I mean, JUST LOOK AT THE COVER! HOW COULD I NOT WANT TO LOVE THIS?! Anyway, I had this period of time where I just decided that I was going to skip this completely, BUT THEN I saw three people give this 3-4 stars and they're all people whose reviews I completely trust... and well I gave in to the cover and read it. Well, I didn't rea</span>
  <span id="freeText43399518078934618" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>Mini review:</b><br /><br />After the early reviews started rolling in for this one I was getting less and less excited about reading this one. I mean, JUST LOOK AT THE COVER! HOW COULD I NOT WANT TO LOVE THIS?! Anyway, I had this period of time where I just decided that I was going to skip this completely, BUT THEN I saw three people give this 3-4 stars and they're all people whose reviews I completely trust... and well I gave in to the cover and read it. Well, I didn't really read it. I more like, barfed through it.<br /><br />I'll give the book this: it was a light and fast read. I was almost finished by no time but then figured that there was no longer any point so I DNFed it after Ash and Violet just started overly-infuriatingly cheesy. (Note that they were already infuriately cheesy and instant-lovey beforehand.) The instant love is actually so bad.<br /><br />This is when they first meet<br /><blockquote>I can only stare. His mouth curves into a full smile and I feel my lungs contract, making it very difficult to breathe.</blockquote><br />And then just moments later when Violet is alone, staring at her beauteous self in the mirror<br /><blockquote>I've never thought much about kissing, but the idea of Ash's lips against mine--<br />I giggle.</blockquote><br />Oh and then later at that night intense staring ensues<br /><blockquote>I look up and meet a pair of bray-green eyes, no longer soft but blazing. Ash doesn't look away, and neither do I. His gaze is fierce, and open, and it makes me feel alive. He isn't looking at a surrogate--he's looking at <em>me. </em></blockquote><br />I mean really, no shit he's looking at you. *eyeroll*<br /><blockquote>It's only been a couple of hours since I met him, but he's somehow even more handsome than I remember. My whole body feels like it's blushing.</blockquote><br />I CAN'T DO THIS ANY LONGER.<br /><br />Anyway, if you like the whole X meets Y thing, the best I can give you is <em>The Hunger Games </em>meets <em>The Selection. </em>That being; the excellent potential of <em>The Hunger Games </em>but actually just as bad as <em>The Selection. </em><br /><br />I'm done here.<br /><br />Celine did a full review on the blog and it's 10000 times better so you should <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/2014/08/review-the-jewel-by-amy-ewing/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">check that out.</a></span>
