    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1046213926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1046213926" />
    <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland"><img alt="Aly (In Wonderland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552929589p2/22178203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1046213926?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (In Wonderland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (In Wonderland)" href="/user/show/22178203-aly-in-wonderland">Aly (In Wonderland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406347494" href="/book/show/22586252-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22178203-aly-in-wonderland?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1046213926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2522448645643764077"><i>
  <blockquote>There are perks to being a surrogate. We get to dress how we want, eat what we want, sleep late on the weekends. We get an education. A good education. We get free food and water, we always have electricity, and we never have to work. We never have to know poverty -- and the caretakers tell us we'll have more once we start living in the Jewel.<br/>Except freedom. They never seem to mention that.</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>For a long while, this was two stars for me. It was good, but not exceptional. It was an innovative ide</span>
  <span id="freeText2522448645643764077" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>There are perks to being a surrogate. We get to dress how we want, eat what we want, sleep late on the weekends. We get an education. A good education. We get free food and water, we always have electricity, and we never have to work. We never have to know poverty -- and the caretakers tell us we'll have more once we start living in the Jewel.<br>Except freedom. They never seem to mention that.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>For a long while, this was two stars for me. It was good, but not exceptional. It was an innovative idea, but not something I hadn't heard before. For a long time, the execution fell flat... until Violet is bought at the Auction and reaches the Jewel, as the new surrogate for the Duchess of the Lake.<br><br>But let's start from the beginning.<br><br>Violet Lasting lives in Southgate. When she became a woman, her blood test showed abnormalities, magical abilities, which meant she was to become a surrogate for the royal families. <br><br>Every woman who has magical abilities becomes a surrogate. They live a sheltered life until they have proven their abilities, and then they are auctioned off. <br><br><i>The Jewel</i> reminded me of <b>The Hunger Games ft. The Selection ft. Eve</b> and I was delighted to find that it's not as bad as everyone makes it out to be. Yes, there's insta-love (but come on, what dystopia <i>doesn't</i> have insta-love?) and yes, the MC, Violet, comes across as <b>a little bit too sheltered at times</b> (she wasn't sure whether sex involved lying down. Really?) but in the context of the story, it worked.<br><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>The Duchess gives some polite response, but the world is suddenly muted as I take in the surrogate attached to the chain.<br>She is hugely pregnant.<br>I can't quite make out her face through the veil, and her eyes are downcast. But she can't be much older than I am.<br>Reality hits me like a block of cement.<br>I'm staring at my future.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>The Jewel put the fear of God in me.</b> That may sound melodramatic, but just imagine it: in the future, all girls between the ages of 11/12 and 18 will not have a future. They will be surrogates for powerful families, and then they will die. And if they aren't magical, they will be destined to live in the slums <b>with no chance to get out.</b> It was creepy, to see all these young girls <b>attached to leashes, chained like dogs, and heavily pregnant.</b> <br><br>And it's even more creepy when you realise that these girls you're growing up with? They're not only your friends, but your sisters, your cousins, any female relative that has an inch of magic in their bodies.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>The girl sniffs and turns to another surrogate, pleading for information. The lioness catches me frowning at her and glares. "What?"<br>"I don't understand you," I say. "She was just looking for help."<br>The lioness laughs. "I don't understand you," she says. "All of you. You act like sniveling weaklings, afraid of your mistresses. WE make their children. WE have the power.</blockquote>
</i><br><br>And in the end, that's what it comes down to: power and there is nothing these women won't do.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>The Duchess raises an eyebrow. "The Electress seems to have forgotten that I have been around much longer than she has. I am descended from one of the four founding Houses, not some shopkeeper in the Bank. She thought she could change the rules. She is a disgrace to the throne, and an embarrassment to her title, and yesterday she learned that no one is untouchable." She glances at my dumbstruck face and her mouth curls into a smirk. "Welcome to the Jewel."</blockquote>
</i><br><br>The Electress (which I assume is the queen of the Jewel) has just had a baby son. Every royal woman is racing to have a baby girl, so that their families can be joined in marriage. And Violet, having the strongest power in <b>growth</b> is being pressured into succeeding...<br><br><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"And this is why the Duchess bought me?" I say. "Because I'm so good at Growth?"<br>"Has she spoken to you already?"<br>I nod. "She gave me a whole list of qualities she wants her baby to have. But I don't know how to do any of it."<br>"Not just that, Violet," Dr. Blythe says. "She wants her daughter to be born first. She believes that, with your abilities, her child can be born much faster than the usual nine months. And it will be... more advanced than your typical infant. You can speed up the developmental process as well as the physical."</blockquote>
</i><br><br>It's a race against time, but Violet is more and more against harming the child that way, especially when she meets Ash, a companion and <b>cue the insta-love.</b><br><br>I knew it was going to happen, and it didn't shock me, and I didn't buy into it. It felt very much like a teenage girl's wet dream, and it did nothing for me, but it helped the plot move along and if this was Ewing's intention, then good for her because it worked.<br><br><b>And am I the only one who wants Violet to end up with Garnet, not Ash?</b> I am so, so, SO over the sweet, pretty boy routine. <i>Boring.</i><br><br>The one thing that annoyed me was how this book <b>quickly became a colour chart.</b> I mean everyone in this book is named after a colour. Don't believe me?<br><br>- <b>Garnet</b>, the Duchesses son.<br>- <b>Violet</b>, the surrogate.<br>- <b>Pearl</b>, the Duchess.<br>- <b>Raven</b>, Violet's best friend.<br>- <b>Sapphire</b>, another Duchess.<br>- <b>Carnelian</b>, the Duchesses niece.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415809731ra/11848839.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WE GET IT. I highly doubt there's a reason behind this and even if there was, I wouldn't care. It's too much. TOO MUCH.<br><br><b>If you don't mind your usual YA dystopia tropes, ie. insta-love, insta-attraction, an impending revolution and pretty surprising plot twists</b> then this is the book for you. It does have all the tropes, and then some. So I highly recommend those who don't want to read something like that to stay away, because it'll annoy me.<br><br>Also, what the hell was with that cliffhanger? WHY? THIS IS NOT OKAY.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2522448645643764077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1878669025" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1878669025" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1878669025?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=help-help-i-m-being-repressed">help-help-i-m-being-repressed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=pretty-cover-sparklies">pretty-cover-sparklies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1878669025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5164501114944187024"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>Don't be fooled by the pretty cover sparklies; THE JEWEL is actually pretty messed-up. Violet lives in a dystopian city that's organized like the nine circles of hell, with the Marsh, or the slums, on the outer rings; and then Farm, the agricultural; Smoke, the industrial; Bank, the financial; and in the very heart of the city is Jewel, where are the filthy rich members of royalty reside.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Violet was born in the Marsh but has been raised i</span>
  <span id="freeText5164501114944187024" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>Don't be fooled by the pretty cover sparklies; THE JEWEL is actually pretty messed-up. Violet lives in a dystopian city that's organized like the nine circles of hell, with the Marsh, or the slums, on the outer rings; and then Farm, the agricultural; Smoke, the industrial; Bank, the financial; and in the very heart of the city is Jewel, where are the filthy rich members of royalty reside.<br><br><br><br>Violet was born in the Marsh but has been raised in relative luxury since puberty because she has the power of "Auguries," or magical abilities which mean her womb is perfect for breeding more members of royalty in the Jewel. This is called being a "Surrogate." When the Surrogates come of age, they are auctioned off in 200 lots, with the last ten being the most desirable of all. Violet is #197, because her magical abilities are so potent.<br><br><br><br>With her new owner, the Duchess of the Lake, Violet now resides in the upper crust of society, receiving expensive gifts, pretty dresses, and fancy feasts - but of course it all comes at a cost. She's treated as an object, paraded around on a leash, and artificially inseminated against her will multiple times, because she's essentially a bejeweled incubator, and not an actual human being. Since this is a YA dystopian, obviously there's a forbidden romance subplot and <i>obviously </i>she is the chosen one who will save humanity of themselves while making out and dressing up and getting into catfights with rivals.<br><br><br><br>THE JEWEL really made some of my friends angry, which, ironically, made me want to read it even more. I can see why, to be honest. The concept of surrogacy in a YA series is so odd, and it was done so badly in this world because the world-building leaves so much to be desired. Is this our world, or a completely different one? Why can they do magic? Why do they have nosebleeds and headache when they do magic? Why can't the rich people conceive? If the rich people can't conceive, why do they need specially trained people to teach them how to have sex and make out? Oh, yes, this book has teen escorts, called "companions" who basically teach the young royals how to seduce and be desirable, with the understanding that they sleep with the older members of the household. What.<br><br><br><br>Furthermore, what are they inseminating the Surrogates with? Is it just the women who are infertile? Why not the men? And if the men are too, where are they getting the sperm from? Are there male donors who are similarly imprisoned? Why don't we see them? And also, what does Surrogate training consist of, because Violet seems <i>remarkably </i>uninformed about sex <i>and </i>pregnancy. <br><br><br><br>Also, the names in this book are ridiculous. Violet's siblings are named Ocher and Hazel. Her friend is named Raven and she has a twin brother named Crow. The members of royalty have names like Sailor Moon villains, like Beryl (an actual Sailor Moon villain fyi), Carnelian, Garnet, and Sapphire.<br><br><br><br>I feel like there was a lot of potential in this book to be great, but considering the subject matter revolves around prostitution, eugenics, lobotomies, and reproductive rights, the tone feels deceptively - almost insultingly - light with all the descriptions of pretty dresses and luxury items, and the weird and totally unconvincing romance between Violet and Ash. It is compulsively readable and reasonably well-written, but I felt like it really glossed over the serious issues and that was not good. HUNGER GAMES and HANDMAID'S TALE were good because they had fully developed worlds (for the most part) and didn't shy away from the grievous consequences of insurrection. THE JEWEL tries, but the emotional disconnect and lack of atmosphere really put a damper on the horror factor.<br><br><br><br>My library has a copy of book two, THE WHITE ROSE, so I'm going to read that and see if this book develops more in the sequel. So far, I probably wouldn't recommend this to anyone unless they enjoy costume dys-trope-ian YA fiction like THE SELECTION that revolves more around romance and boys than social commentary.<br><br><br><br>1.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5164501114944187024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

It's not believable and it's so hard to connect with that.<br><br>Over all THE JEWEL is sloppy writing, lackluster "shallow" characters, a complete nonsensical.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857759846" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430689841p2/8769426.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/8769426-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=physical-arc">physical-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8769426-ashley?shelf=bea14">bea14</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857759846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1408472782471204276"><b><a href='http://www.nosegraze.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nose Graze</a> — Book reviews & blogging tips</b><br/><br/><em>
  <strong>The Jewel</strong>
</em> was an awesome book! ...until the romance. But more on that later. ;)<br/><br/>I really loved the plot in The Jewel. I think it's definitely similar in vibe to <a href='http://www.nosegraze.com/the-selection-by-kiera-cass/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Selection</a> (which it's being compared to). However, my feelings about it are the total opposite. In The Selection, I adored the romance but didn't care much about the rest of the plot. In The Jewel, I adore the plot but hate the romance. The Jewel has a lot of political/royal scandal.. and i</span>
  <span id="freeText1408472782471204276" style="display:none"><b><a href="http://www.nosegraze.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Nose Graze</a> — Book reviews &amp; blogging tips</b><br /><br /><em>
  <strong>The Jewel</strong>
</em> was an awesome book! ...until the romance. But more on that later. ;)<br /><br />I really loved the plot in The Jewel. I think it's definitely similar in vibe to <a href="http://www.nosegraze.com/the-selection-by-kiera-cass/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection</a> (which it's being compared to). However, my feelings about it are the total opposite. In The Selection, I adored the romance but didn't care much about the rest of the plot. In The Jewel, I adore the plot but hate the romance. The Jewel has a lot of political/royal scandal.. and it's fascinating! Everyone is basically frenemies. The royals invite each other over for tea parties and dinners, but they actually hate each other and plot against each other.<br /><br />Also, the whole idea of surrogates was HORRIBLE! ..but in a good way. Like obviously it was sad and disgusting, but that's what made the book so interesting. I mean, the girls are bid on at auction, purchased, given collars, walked around on leashes, compared as if they're trophies or trading cards (bragging about "stats" or talents their surrogates have), etc. That whole part of the book was really disgusting, but fascinating. I was outraged and felt so sorry for Violet! I love that the book got me so riled up.<br /><br />My only gripe with the plot side of things was I didn't fully understand why the surrogates existed. It was only briefly explained why the royals couldn't have their own children. The author explained how their children died early or were sickly, etc., but I didn't fully understand WHY.<br /><br />But then somewhere around page 250, the romance kicked in.. and it sucked. Violet meets this guy Ash, they exchange about two glances, then his lips are on hers, then they're making out, then they're saying "I love you". They have like three interactions, zero conversations, and they're already in love? Waaaa??? I was really disappointed because there could have been a lot of potential with this romance, but it was easily the weakest part of the book. I didn't connect with it at all. I went from being addicted to The Jewel to kind of making a "wtf" face at it while reading.<br /><br />I was pretty devastated to have my love for this book plummet so hard, because up until that point, I was ADDICTED. I read the whole thing in less than 24 hours. I loved it so much, then the romance just sucked! WHY DID YOU DO THIS TO ME?!?!<br /><br />But the book is still worth reading, even if just for the cool plot and crazy political scandals. The different houses of royalty are constantly plotting against each other and it's pretty crazy what lengths they go to!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1408472782471204276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1828000591?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddie" href="/user/show/18523225-maddie">Maddie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406347494" href="/book/show/22586252-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1828000591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11134302071416339609">This was the perfect dystopian style book for me. I love The Selection by Keira Cass and Wither by Lauren DeStefano, and The Jewel fits perfectly into that category of girl-in-pretty-dresses-doing-badass-things. I thought the Lone City itself was well explained and easy to imagine, and the magic system was simple to grasp. The concept of surrogates made a lot of sense, but the actual 'how?' behind the procedure is what's tripping me up. <br/><br/>I was also warned about the insta-love in this book, and ye</span>
  <span id="freeText11134302071416339609" style="display:none">This was the perfect dystopian style book for me. I love The Selection by Keira Cass and Wither by Lauren DeStefano, and The Jewel fits perfectly into that category of girl-in-pretty-dresses-doing-badass-things. I thought the Lone City itself was well explained and easy to imagine, and the magic system was simple to grasp. The concept of surrogates made a lot of sense, but the actual 'how?' behind the procedure is what's tripping me up. <br /><br />I was also warned about the insta-love in this book, and yes, the relationship between Ash and Violet does escalate from just meeting to 'I can't live without you' pretty quickly, but if Romeo and Juliet can get away with it after all these years, I'll forgive it. It's the kind of romance that I either love or hate and it's just lucky that I loved it this time round! <br /><br />I'm beyond pumped to read the next book in the series now that everything's kicking off, and hopefully I can finish the trilogy by the end of the year!<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1047408522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1047408522" />
    <a title="☙ nemo ❧" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19742661-nemo"><img alt="☙ nemo ❧" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604079632p2/19742661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1047408522?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☙ nemo ❧" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☙ nemo ❧" href="/user/show/19742661-nemo">☙ nemo ❧</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406347494" href="/book/show/22586252-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=ya-hall-of-fame">ya-hall-of-fame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=physical-books-i-own">physical-books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=romance-erotica-mf">romance-erotica-mf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19742661-nemo?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1047408522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9687611115346040536">So, I wasn't originally going to write a review for this, since I guess I'm not really a review-writing sort of person. But then I saw the overwhelmingly bad reviews, and I felt sorry for this book - which I thought was actually rather good - getting so much negative attention.<br/><br/>First of all, I didn't have tremendously high hopes upon starting this book. I expected it to be mediocre at best, and awfully problematic and rage-inducing at worst. To my surprise, it was actually far better than I was e</span>
  <span id="freeText9687611115346040536" style="display:none">So, I wasn't originally going to write a review for this, since I guess I'm not really a review-writing sort of person. But then I saw the overwhelmingly bad reviews, and I felt sorry for this book - which I thought was actually rather good - getting so much negative attention.<br /><br />First of all, I didn't have tremendously high hopes upon starting this book. I expected it to be mediocre at best, and awfully problematic and rage-inducing at worst. To my surprise, it was actually far better than I was expecting!<br /><br /><b>Things I Liked:</b><br /><br />- Female friendship! There was genuine, real friendship between Violet and her best friend Raven, as well as some other girls in the novel. It's great to see non-duplicitous friendships in YA novels between girls! I hate it when the heroine's only friends are either a boy or girls who she's only pretending to like.<br /><br />- Characterisation! I've heard a lot of people complaining about Violet being whiny, but I completely disagree. I really do not see how she is whiny at all. She was a strong character, rebelling against her mistress whenever she could but clever enough to be submissive when she had to be, to gain her mistress's trust. She did complain sometimes, but never enough to be excessive - and she had just been sold at auction, as property, and was going to be forced to carry someone else's child. Isn't a bit of complaining <i>justified</i> in such circumstances? Gosh. I also liked the Duchess of the Lake's character - it would have been so easy to make her shallow and overwhelmingly-evil, but instead we see other sides of her that are rather unexpected, and add to her complexity as a character.<br /><br />- VIOLET. I mentioned this in the last point, but I really did like Violet. She <i>was</i> a strong female character, and she wasn't afraid to acknowledge her beauty - something which I also found refreshing, as a lot of YA heroines think of themselves as plain until some boy comes along and then suddenly she realises she's pretty, but this wasn't the case with Violet at all. The fact that she's named after her eye colour is a bit cheesy though, I must admit that.<br /><br /><b>Things I Was Uncertain Whether I Liked Or Not:</b><br /><br />- The Auguries. Whereas it did add a touch of originality and magic to the story (and I do have a very large weakness for magic), it wasn't really explained <i>why</i> the surrogates had this power, and as such it felt a little out of place. <br /><br />- The Worldbuilding. It was great in some parts: we learn about the royal houses and how the Lone City is arranged and who does what and what goes where, but shaky in other parts. The Lone City is surrounded by water - are we to assume it is an island? Are there any other countries that are lurking beyond the sea, or is the sea too perilous to even try and venture past? And, of course, we still know next-to-nothing about the Auguries. <br /><br /><b>Things I Didn't Really Like:</b><br /><br />- The romance. It wasn't as bad as some I've seen, and it wasn't abusive like in certain other YA books <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[*cough* Hush Hush *cough* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but there was a definite element of insta-love about it, and it went far too fast to really be believable. But it wasn't super-terrible, at least. <br /><br />So this wasn't a perfect book, by any means, and there wasn't really much in the way of diversity either (although it wasn't devoid of diversity altogether, there was still much to be desired). But I don't think it was a bad book, by any definition of the term, and if you're contemplating reading this book but are put off by the negative reviews, I would say... just go for it!<br /><br />-<br /><br />edit 22/06/2018: i don't have anything profound to add i'm just laughing at how 4 years ago i "wasn't a review person" and now i review like everything djsjdjsdksd character development</span>
  <a data-text-id="9687611115346040536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer11228528935374440543"><blockquote> <b> "Violet, they do not tell you anything at Southgate. They do not even allow you to look at yourself in the mirror. The less you know, the less identity you have, the easier you are to control." </b> </blockquote><br/>Initially, I picked up this book because I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_' title='The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Selection</a> and I was not disappointed. I've been thinking about rereading this series for quite some time now and the second time around didn't diappoint either. <br/>The writing is really good, the story gripping and the world Amy Ewing built here, is pur</span>
  <span id="freeText11228528935374440543" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b> "Violet, they do not tell you anything at Southgate. They do not even allow you to look at yourself in the mirror. The less you know, the less identity you have, the easier you are to control." </b> </blockquote><br />Initially, I picked up this book because I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_" title="The Selection (The Selection, #1) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection</a> and I was not disappointed. I've been thinking about rereading this series for quite some time now and the second time around didn't diappoint either. <br />The writing is really good, the story gripping and the world Amy Ewing built here, is purely fascinating. Brutal and evil, behind all the glitter. Plus, I really like Violet. This time around, I can't give five stars anymore though. There are some weaknesses and this time I found myself shaking my head at some points of the story. But it wasn't enough to stop me enjoying this book and I'm really looking forward to continue the reread.</span>

<div id="review_792036071" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/792036071" />
    <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page"><img alt="Danielle (Love at First Page)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578285312p2/1312450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/792036071?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (Love at First Page)" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page">Danielle (Love at First Page)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=own-kindle-book">own-kindle-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=genre-young-adult">genre-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=fantasy-scifi-paranormal">fantasy-scifi-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer792036071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5443862909493763937"><b>Edit: Screw it. I'm bumping the rating up after thinking about the book all day! <br/><br/>3.5-4 stars</b><br/><br/>Hey, now, this is an enjoyable book *and* romance! (I see you judging me. Haters to the left.) I will gladly say that <i>The Jewel</i> is very, very readable and addicting. From start to finish, I was glued to the pages. Maybe it's not wholly unique (a few too many things reminded me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_' title='The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hunger Games</a>), yet the premise is interesting and has potential. The idea of girls being raised as surrogates for the highe</span>
  <span id="freeText5443862909493763937" style="display:none"><b>Edit: Screw it. I'm bumping the rating up after thinking about the book all day! <br /><br />3.5-4 stars</b><br /><br />Hey, now, this is an enjoyable book *and* romance! (I see you judging me. Haters to the left.) I will gladly say that <i>The Jewel</i> is very, very readable and addicting. From start to finish, I was glued to the pages. Maybe it's not wholly unique (a few too many things reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>), yet the premise is interesting and has potential. The idea of girls being raised as surrogates for the higher echelon of society is terrifying. Really, my main complaint would be the fantasy aspect to the worldbuilding, which I don't understand at all. See, the surrogates have command of the "Auguries", meaning they can change things by color, shape, and size. Born with this mutation, these girls from the poorer side of town have become the highest commodity since it means they can be impregnated and produce healthy offspring, which the royal women can no longer do. There is absolutely zero explanation for how this has happened or how it's even possible. It defies logic and feels completely random. I'm hoping the next book at least attempts more clarification, but as it stands, I wish that part was left out entirely. <br /><br />Back on the plus side, I liked Violet, the main character, much more than I expected to. She's caring and has a good heart, but she's not a doormat in the least. I love how passionate she could be (the cello scene was beautiful), and that she stuck up for herself in small ways. She's strong in her convictions, not once wavering in the belief that, if she stays in the Jewel, she'll lose her freedom and freewill forever. Is she a little naive at times? Sure, but look how this girl was raised! Taken away at a young age, kept in a sterile building, and given very little information about what her life would be like with the royals... I can cut her some slack. She's an admirable and easy to like heroine, I think. The other characters don't have as much depth, but I felt something for all of them - Raven (more of her, please), Ash (a sweetheart, but also a character I want to know better), Annabelle (Violet's mute lady-in-waiting), Garnet (cannot resist the token drunk, charming boy), and the Duchess (*shudders*). And, yeah, okay, there is definitely insta-love going on and some cheesiness, but I was mostly on board with Ash and Violet's romance. When you like someone for the first time, especially at that age, there is going to be some infatuation. While I wish it hadn't moved so quickly, there are good, swoony scenes between them. No love triangle!<br /><br />Soooo, I will definitely be reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24585267.The_White_Rose__The_Lone_City___2_" title="The White Rose (The Lone City, #2) by Amy Ewing" rel="nofollow noopener">The White Rose</a> ASAP. I know many bloggers didn't care for <i>The Jewel</i>, but if you haven't read it yet I'd reconsider. It's, at the very least, an enjoyable, perfectly paced story. <br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.loveatfirstpage.org/2015/07/22/mini-reviews-15/" rel="nofollow noopener">Love at First Page</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5443862909493763937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_879064991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/879064991" />
    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/879064991?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil (or bleed)" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed">Neil (or bleed)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer879064991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer724364076117848740"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/>I want to give it a solid 3 stars because I liked it as a whole. But when I remembered the romance.... okay I don't like to remember that, I toned down my rating to 2.5.<br/><br/>The Jewel would be a definitely good read if the romance was inserted in a good manner or executed well or didn't exist at all. Damn insta-love. This romance has a plot-slaying magic that annoyed me in so many levels. The girl protagonist was overly attached to the guy that she can't control herself to see the guy of her dream</span>
  <span id="freeText724364076117848740" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br /><br />I want to give it a solid 3 stars because I liked it as a whole. But when I remembered the romance.... okay I don't like to remember that, I toned down my rating to 2.5.<br /><br />The Jewel would be a definitely good read if the romance was inserted in a good manner or executed well or didn't exist at all. Damn insta-love. This romance has a plot-slaying magic that annoyed me in so many levels. The girl protagonist was overly attached to the guy that she can't control herself to see the guy of her dreams and flirt with him.<br /><br />The idea of the book is actually good for me (maybe because I haven't read anything like this before) and it became complicated and engaging because of the dystopian atmosphere, paranormal stuff, and the dread from the wicked antagonists and their plans and deceits to overthrow one another and get the power they want. And the writing is decent and easy to read.<br /><br />The dystopian features of this book are actually typical. The world has been divided into 5 groups or 5 Circles that is probably based on caste system. Anyway, I appreciate that it has been explained well.<br /><br />I did buy the paranormal stuff in this which is the Augury. The surrogates can change sizes, shapes and colors of things but there is physical consequences when they're doing this. That's great and it showed that power need not to be abused. At first, I've got wary about this because I felt like it was just an additive to make the story more interesting but later on, after explaining the origin of that magic and laid its essence, well I recognized the full worth of it.<br /><br />The wicked characters which is the Duchess and the other duchess, ladies, electress or the royal women in this book is one of the main reasons why I've been enthralled to read and read this book. I feared them. I hated them. I liked them. At the same time. I don't know exactly why but I think their characters were well-built and interested me more. And I'm really intrigued on they're individual plans on how to get the royal power they wanted.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1615040227?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lolo&#39;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lolo&#39;" href="/user/show/52888957-lolo">lolo&#39;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062235794" href="/book/show/16068780-the-jewel">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615040227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5778276682557149283">Hooray for cliffhanger endings.... <br/><br/>I feel very 50/50 towards this book. I love Violet, Raven, Annabelle, Ash, and Garnet. <br/><br/>But other than that I pretty much despise the whole surrogacy thing and the power moves. And all that is done to the girls disgusts me.<br/><br/>I did enjoy the dialogue. Certain parts were perfectly swell.<br/><br/>It's just hard to look over what makes this book a dystopian. <br/><br/>I love the writing though. <br/><br/>And those last 70 pages were amazing and the reason why I gave it 3 stars. <br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0PaP8JszGMyf9c7gBxVLtDbHd/IJP5G6slMieHRr5/yoZW3mY9pxhz+I4oOkuKZwQYguAyxb4SNKHzHElCpCxQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mIzAipF+qa4G7e8QkT8yIzeWN5c6DtJcRpDCu6TVyEXgHyKcaZfA5aaQw3Mykt/nQNluZh9qosW+3NEHRJRtfA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11476835621687060132">Amy Ewing is the young adult author of <i>The Jewel</i>, the first in a trilogy from HarperTeen, coming out September 2014.<br/><br/>She grew up in a small town outside Boston, where her librarian mother instilled a deep love of reading at a young age. Amy moved to New York City in 2000 to study theater at New York University. Unfortunately, her acting career didn’t quite pan out. She worked in restaurants, as an </span>
  <span id="freeText11476835621687060132" style="display:none">Amy Ewing is the young adult author of <i>The Jewel</i>, the first in a trilogy from HarperTeen, coming out September 2014.<br /><br />She grew up in a small town outside Boston, where her librarian mother instilled a deep love of reading at a young age. Amy moved to New York City in 2000 to study theater at New York University. Unfortunately, her acting career didn’t quite pan out. She worked in restaurants, as an administrative assistant, a nanny, and a sales representative for a wine distributor before the lack of creativity in her life drove her to begin writing.<br /><br />Amy received her MFA in Creative Writing for Children from The New School, where she was lucky enough to meet a fabulous community of YA writers who keep her sane on a daily basis. She lives in Harlem, where she spends her days writing, eating cheese, and occasionally binge watching The Vampire Diaries. </span>
